; hitopadesha-slp1_p.txt
; Begun 07-24-2019 as copy of hitopadesha-slp1.txt
; Incorporates the 'marma-prakASikA' commentary of Kale -- these are
; the Sanskrit notes at the bottom of each page.
; These notes are inserted below the Analyzed Sandhi lines
; Format is ###.##P: <slp1 text>
;  There may be more than one ###.##P line, if a given line of text has
;  comments on more than one word. For example, see line 001.04 below.
; Also, use ###.##PE: <English translation of the prakASikA>
; ------------------------------------------------
; A convention of this file is that lines starting with semicolon are comments
; Begun approx. Apr 2016
; Each line is represented in two forms:
;  F  is the final sandhi form; this is the version one sees printed
;  A  is the analyzed sandhi form.  Here words are separated, if needed,
;     and word endings are changed to their original (pre-sandhi) form.
;     This step of analysis facilitates the further analysis of grammatical
;     form
; ------------------------------------------------------------------
; 2018-12-02   hitokale_slp1_v0.txt
; Begin a new phase. Previous version hitopadesha-slp1.txt
;  The aim now is to use the exact text of Kale's edition:
;      The Hitopadesha of Narayana by M.R. Kale,
;      6th edition Aug 15, 1967. Motilal Banarsidass.
; Reason: We have previously been using the version from Sanskrit Documents (SD)
;   website  (reference elsewhere: TODO)
; However, there are various differences between Kale's version and this
; version.  These differences make difficult the correlation between
; the Sanskrit text and Kale's English translation.
; Large chunks of the SD text are identical to Kale, but many small and
; some large variances appear.  I've been handling these differences in
; various ways, but am now thinking that it would be better to have the
; text of Kale exactly.
; The line numbers of form #### currently relate to the original SD document.
; Preliminary format of Kale line numbers will be as '###.##'  (page.line)
; and some lines will have form '###.## ####' with both line numbers.
; Kale's comments at the bottom of pages are NOT included currently.
; ------------------------------------------------------------------
; hitokale_slp1_v1.txt  12/25/2018
; This replaces the xxxxF: or xxxxA: line numbering of original hitopadesha-slp1.txt
; Instead, the line numbering PPP.LLF: (or PPP.LLF:) is used.
; The PPP is Kale page number, and is believed to agree with the page number of the Kale text.
; The line number (LL) is less accurately related to the lines of a page of Kale text.
; The difference is believed to be almost entirely within the 'prose' (non-verse) sections.
; Also, the verse text should almost entirely correspond to the Kale text.
; In particular, the verse numbering should agree;
; and the number of lines per verse should agree  (most verses take 2 lines, and the
; second line has the verse number at the end (form .. VVV .. ; sometimes the space between
; V and ending '..' is missing).
; PA :  sandhi analyzed form of marma-prakASikA
; ° : marker for undisplayed text.
; ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
; in anuzwup,  
; akzara (syllable) 5 is light in all 4 padas
; akzara 6 is heavy in all 4 padas
; akzara 7 is light in  padas 1 and 3, but heavy in padas 2 and 4
; https://www.learnsanskrit.org/tools/sanscript/
; NOTE: śloka means anuṣṭup śloka 
; श्लोके षष्ठं गुरु ज्ञेयं सर्वत्र लघु पञ्चमम्।
; द्विचतुष्पादयोर्ह्रस्वं सप्तमं दीर्घमन्ययोः॥
; śloke ṣaṣṭhaṃ guru jñeyaṃ sarvatra laghu pañcamam।
; dvicatuṣpādayorhrasvaṃ saptamaṃ dīrghamanyayoḥ॥
;  or ? dvicatuḥpādayorhrasvaṃ
; ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

;
001.01F: .. hitopadeSaH ..
001.01A: .. hita-upadeSaH ..
; hita good, useful; upadeSa advice
001.01P: hitasya upadeSaH: hitopadeSaH . hitaScAsO upadeSaSca iti vA . sa eva lakzaRayA tatsaMjYaH granTaH .
;001.01PA: hitasya upadeSaH: hitopadeSaH . hitaH ca asO upadeSaH ca iti vA . saH eva lakzaRayA tatsaMjYaH granTaH .

001.02F: prastAvikA
001.02A: prastAvikA
; prastu = stu to praise
; prastAva introduction; prastAvikA same sense but not in dictionaries
001.01-02E: Good advice.  Introduction.

001.03F: sidDiH sADye satAmastu prasAdAt tasya DUrjaweH .
001.03A: sidDiH sADye satAm astu prasAdAt tasya DUrjaweH .
; sidDi success; sADya an object to be accomplished;
; sat good person; prasAda grace (graciousness)
; DUr in comp. for Dur; Dur burden, top; jawi twisted hair (dreadlocks?)
; DUrjawi N. of Rudra-Siva
001.03P: DUH BAraBUtA jawA yasya asO DUrjawiH . tasya DUrjaweH prasAdAt satAM sADye aBimatavizaye sidDiH astu .

001.04F: jAhnavIPenaleKeva yanmUrDni SaSinaH kalA .. 1..
001.04A: jAhnavI-Pena-leKA iva yad-mUrDni SaSinaH kalA .. 1..
; jahnu ; jAhnavI daughter of jahnu (= gaNgA) ; Pena foam; leKa scratch, drawing
; SaSin containing a hare (= moon);
; kalA a small part, a digit or 1/16 of moon's diameter
001.04P: jAhnavI-Pena-leKeva -- jahnoH apatyaM strI jAhnavI tasyA Penasya leKA .
;001.04PA: jAhnavIPenaleKA iva -- jahnoH apatyam strI jAhnavI tasyAH Penasya leKA .
001.04P: yanmUrDni -- yasya mUrDA yanmUrDA tasmin .

001.03-04E: May success attend the good in their undertakings (in the object they wish to accomplish) by the favour of that Dhurjati, on whose head there is a digit of the moon looking like a streak of the foam of the Ganges.

001.05F: Sruto hitopadeSo'yaM pAwavaM saMskftoktizu .
001.05A: SrutaH hitopadeSaH ayam pAwavam saMskfta-uktizu .
; Sruta heard, studied; pAwava sharpness, cleverness
; saMskft used as name of language by daRqin in daSakumAracarita (800 CE).
001.05P: SrutaH samyagaDItaH ityarTaH .
;001.05PA: SrutaH samyak aDItaH iti arTaH .
001.05P: pAwavaM -- pawoH BAvaH .

001.06F: vAcAM sarvatra vEcitryaM nItividyAM dadAti ca .. 2..
001.06A: vAcAm sarvatra vEcitryam nItividyAm dadAti ca .. 2..
; vEcitrya variety (citra = vicitra = various, diverse)
; nIti wise conduct, political science.
001.06P: vEcitryam -- vicitrasya BAvaH .
001.06P: nItividyAm -- nItiSAstrajYAnam .

001.05-06E: This Hitopadesa (the work inculcating salutary instruction) when studied (lit., carefully attended to) gives (the student) proficiency in elegant speeches, a variety of expression in every department and a knowledge of the conduct of human affairs.
;
; 05-16-2022
;
001.07F: ajarAmaravat prAjYo vidyAmarTaM ca cintayet .
001.07A: ajara-amara-vat prAjYaH vidyAm arTam ca cintayet .
; a-jara ageless; amara immortal; prAjYa wise man
; vidyA knowledge; arTa wealth
001.07P: ajarAmaravat -- jarayA nizkrAntaH ajaraH , nAsti jarA yasya iti vA . na mriyate asO amaraH ca ajarAmaraH tena tulyam .

001.08F: gfhIta iva keSezu mftyunA DarmamAcaret .. 3..
001.08A: gfhItaH iva keSezu mftyunA Darmam Acaret .. 3..
; Darma good works, duties; Acar to practice

002.07-08E: A wise man should think of (acquiring) knowledge and money as though he were not subject to old age or death: but he should perform his religious duties as if Death had seized him by the hair.

001.09F: sarvadravyezu vidyEva dravyamAhuranuttamam .
001.09A: sarvadravyezu vidyA eva dravyam AhuH an-uttamam .
; dravya A thing, a possession, wealth;
; anuttama unsurpassed (bahuvrihi)
001.09P: anuttamam -- nAsti uttamam yasmAt .

001.10F: ahAryatvAdanarGyatvAdakzayatvAcca sarvadA .. 4..
001.10A: a-hArya-tvAt an-arGya-tvAt a-kzaya-tvAt ca sarvadA .. 4..
; hArya to be taken away; a-hArya-tva (non-stealable-ness - cannot be stolen);
; arGya price; an-arGya-tva pricelessness; sarvadA always
; a-kzaya-tva non-decaying-ness
001.10P: ahAryatvAt -- hartuM yogyaM SakyaM vA na BavatIti ahAryaM tasya BAvaH ahAryatvam . evam anarGyatvAdi .

001.09-10E: Learning, of all things, (the wise) declare to be without a superior (the best of them all ), because of its incapability of being taken away, or valued or exhausted.

; Muller has saMgamayati. 
001.11F: saMyojayati vidyEva nIcagApi naraM sarit .
001.11A: saMyojayati vidyA eva nIcagA api naram sarit .
; saMyuj to join; nIca ni (down) +aYc; nIca-ga going low; sarit river
; implicit nIcagam
001.11P: vidyA eva nIcagApi [satI] naraM durDarzaM nfpaM saMyojayati nIcagApi sarit durDarzaM samudramiva .
;
;
; Muller uses 'durDarzaM', which makes more sense; this text so changed.
; Kale also 'durDarzaM'
001.12F: samudramiva durDarzaM nfpaM BAgyamataH param .. 5..
001.12A: samudram iva durDarzam nfpam BAgyam ataH param .. 5..
; samudra ocean; Dfz to be bold, to assail; dur-Darza inaccessible
; BAgya good fortune; ataH thence; para highest.
001.12P: durdarzamiti pAWaH . ataH nfpAtsamudrAcca paraM mahat BAgyaM ataHparaM narasya BAgyamiti vA .

001.11-12E: Learning, although possessed by a low man, introduces him to the king who is (ordinarily) inapproachable, just as a river, although flowing through a low region, takes one to the inaccessible sea : (sources) from which floweth great fortune (or, the future rests with fortune).

; 05-17-2022

001.13F: vidyA dadAti vinayaM vinayAdyAti pAtratAm .
001.13A: vidyA dadAti vinayam vinayAt yAti pAtra-tAm .
; vinaya modesty; pAtra vessel, capability; pAtra-tA worthiness (competence), eligibility
001.13P: vidyeti -- atra kAraRamAlAlaMkAraH .
001.13P+: tallakzaRaM yaTA -- yaTottaraM cetpUrvasya pUrvasyArTasya hetutA . tadA kAraRamAlA syAt. kA . pra . (sAhi . da . 10.76)
; MW kAraRa-mAlA = 'a series or chain of causes' ref. sAhitya-dArpaRa

001.14F: pAtratvAdDanamApnoti DanAdDarmaM tataH suKam .. 6..
001.14A: pAtratvAt Danam Apnoti DanAt Darmam tataH suKam .. 6..
; Darma religious merit;

001.13-14E: Learning endows one with modesty ; from (having) modesty one passes on to (gets) worthiness ; being worthy one obtains riches ; from riches religious merit and from that happiness.

001.15F: vidyA Sastrasya SAstrasya dve vidye pratipattaye .
001.15A: vidyA Sastrasya SAstrasya dve vidye pratipattaye .
; Sastra weapon; SAstra scripture (?)
; pattaye case 4s; prati-patti fame (ap90), action (?) 'conduce to glory'?
001.15P: Sastrasya vidyA , SAstrasya vidyA , ete dve vidye pratipattaye kIrtaye BavataH .

001.16F: AdyA hAsyAya vfdDatve dvitIyAdriyate sadA .. 7..
; Kale typo: ditIyA -> dvitIyA
001.16A: AdyA hAsyAya vfdDatve dvitIyA A-driyate sadA .. 7..
; AdyA Adi (f. 1s) first; dvitIya 2nd; A-df pres. pass. 3s to respect

001.15-16E: The knowledge of arms and that of the Sastras - these two lores conduce to glory: but the former exposes one to ridicule in old age, while the latter is ever respected.

001.17F: yannave BAjane lagnaH saMskAro nAnyaTA Bavet .
001.17A: yad nave BAjane lagnaH saMskAraH na anyaTA Bavet .
; yad as; nava new; BAjana vessel, pot; lagna attached (lag to adhere)
; saMskAra impression (put together)
001.17P: yaTA nave BAjane AmaBAjane ityarTaH .
; Ama raw, unbaked
; pracyAvayitum, pramArzwum ? inf. of what?  causal infinitives of pracyu
001.17P+: lagnaH saMskAraH anyaTA na Bavet svasTAnAtpracyAvayituM pramArzwuM vA na Sakyate
001.18F: kaTAcCalena bAlAnAM nItistadiha kaTyate .. 8..
001.18A: kaTAcCalena bAlAnAm nItiH tad iha kaTyate .. 8..
; kaTA-Cala story-guise; nIti science of conduct; tad so
001.18P: taTA bAlA api nItimaDyApitAScetsA tezAM cetasi dfQaM padaM kuryAditi hetoH sA kaTAmizeRa bAlAnAmiha kaTyate  .
;001.18PA: taTA bAlAH api nItim aDyApitAH cet sA tezAm cetasi dfQam padam kuryAt iti hetoH sA kaTAmizeRa bAlAnAm iha kaTyate .

001.17-18E: As an impression made upon a raw (earthen or so) pot can undergo no change afterwards -- so (following the same principle) in this work the science of conduct (or policy) is taught to youths under the guise of stories.

; 05-18-2022

002.01F: mitralABaH suhfdBedo vigrahaH saMDireva ca .
002.01A: mitra-lABaH suhfdBedaH vigrahaH saMDiH eva ca .
; mitra-lABa obtaining friend; suhfd-Beda separation (breaking);
; vigraha separation, war; saMDi alliance, peace.

002.02F: paYcatantrAttaTAnyasmAdgranTAdAkfzya liKyate .. 9..
002.02A: paYcatantrAt taTA anyasmAt granTAt Akfzya liKyate .. 9..
; granTa literary production; Akfz to extract (kfz to drag, plough)
; taTA similarly
002.01-02E:   [The subjects of] "The acquisition of friends", "The separation of friends", "Making war" and "Concluding peace" are written upon, extracts being made from Panchatantra and other works.

002.03F: asti BAgIraTItIre pAwaliputranAmaDeyaM nagaram . tatra sarvasvAmiguRopetaH sudarSano
002.03A: asti BAgIraTI-tIre pAwali-putra-nAmaDeyam nagaram . tatra sarva-(svAmi-guRa)-upetaH sudarSanaH
; BagIraTa 'have a glorious chariot' (vAlmiki rAmayaRa). In India there are several ramayanas!
; pAwali (a red flower) is like a son to the place.
; BAgIraTI name of a river, perhaps the Ganges; tIra a shore;
; svAmi ruler, master; guRa attribute; upeta endowed with
; su-darSana (proper name) easily seen, keen sighted
002.03P: sarvasvAmi -- svAminaH guRAH svAmiguRAH . sarve ca te svAmiguRASca (karma) tEH upetaH .
002.03P+: (tf. ta.) sudarSanaH -- SoBanaM darSanaM yasya (bahu.) .

002.04F: nAma narapatirAsIt . sa BUpatirekadA kenApi pAWyamAnaM SlokadvayaM SuSrAva --
002.04A: nAma nara-patiH AsIt . saH BUpatiH ekadA kena api pAWyamAnam Sloka-dvayam SuSrAva --
; nara-pati lord of men, king. BU-pati lord of earth;
; pAWyamAna ca. ppr. ps. paW (Huet) being recited.
; Sloka-dvaya a pair of shlokas (verses)

002.03-04E: On the bank of the Bhagirathi there is a city named Pataliputra. In it there was a king, Sudarshana by name, endowed with all princely qualities. That king once heard a couple of Slokas (stanzas) chanted by some one ; (viz.)

002.05F: anekasaMSayocCedi parokzArTasya darSakam .
002.05A: aneka-saMSaya-ucCedi parokza-arTasya darSakam .
; aneka many; saMSaya doubt; ucCedin cutting off.
; darSaka seeing;  para, away and akza ifc. for akzi, eye;
; arTa thing, object;  parokza-arTa imperceptible object
002.05P: anekasaM° -- aneke ca te saMSayAH tAn ucCettuM SIlamasya .
002.05P+: parokzArTasya -- akzRoH paraH parokzaH tasya .

002.06F: sarvasya locanaM SAstraM yasya nAstyanDa eva saH .. 10..
002.06A: sarvasya locanam SAstram yasya na asti anDaH eva saH .. 10..
; SAstra = Sruti (Veda) + smfti (Darma-SAstra) +  purARa (incl. itihAsa =  rAmayaRa + mahABArata)))
; locana (loc to see) the eye; anDa blind

002.05-06E: He who does not possess (a knowledge of) Sastra, the universal eye, which totally removes various doubts and discusses things hidden from view, is surely blind.

; 05-20-2022
;
002.07F: yOvanaM DanasampattiH praButvamavivekitA .
002.07A: yOvanam Dana-sampattiH praBu-tvam avivekitA .
; yOvana youth; Dana-sampatti wealth attainment;
; praBu-tva king-ness, powerful-ness;
; vic to divide, discriminate; vivekin judicious;
; vivekitA discrimination, a-vivekitA lack of discrimination
002.07P: yOvaneti -- vayorUpaviBUtInAmekEkaM madakAraRam . iti samAnArTaH SlokAMSaH raGuvaMSe (sa. 17. Slo 13.)

; kim -> kimu  (Kale print smudge).
002.08F: ekEkamapyanarTAya kimu yatra catuzwayam .. 11..
002.08A: ekEkam api anarTAya kimu yatra catuzwayam .. 11..
; kim-u how much more?
; eka-eka one by one; an-arTa dangerous (worthless object, misfortune); yatra where
; catuzwaya group of four
002.07-08E: Youth, abundance of wealth, sovereignty and inconsiderateness are the source of calamity even singly; what then, where all these four are combined !

002.09F: ityAkarRyAtmanaH putrARAmanaDigataSAstrARAM nityamunmArgagAminAM
002.09A: iti AkarRya AtmanaH putrARAm an-aDigata-SAstrARAm nityam unmArga-gAminAM
; aDigata studied; unmArga wrong-path  (ut = out, cf. ucCinna cut 'out')
002.09P: anaDigata -- anaDigatAni anaDItAni SAstrARi yEH .
002.09P+: unmArgagAminAM -- udgataH mArgaH unmArgaH tena gantuM SIlaM yezAM .

002.10F: SAstrAnanuzWAnenodvignamanAH sa rAjA cintayAmAsa .
002.10A: SAstra-an-anuzWAnena udvigna-manAH saH rAjA cintayAmAsa .
; anuzWAna practice,; vij to shake, udvigna-manas whose mind was 'shaken' 
002.10P: SAstrAnanuzWAnena -- SAstrasya ananuzWAnaM SAstrAjYollaMGanaM tena svEravartanena iti yAvat .

002.09-10E: On hearing this, the king, who was distracted at heart, on account of the non-attendance to (the commands of the) Sastras of his sons who had no knowledge of the Sastras and who always followed the wrong path, thought to himself:

002.11F: ko'rTaH putreRa jAtena yo na vidvAn na DArmikaH .
002.11A: kaH arTaH putreRa jAtena yaH na vidvAn na DArmikaH .
; arTa purpose; jAta born; (Why case 3?)
; vidvAn wise (nom. s. m. of vidvas (in Huet declension as 'part'?))
; DArmika righteous

002.12F: kARena cakzuzA kiMvA cakzuHpIqEva kevalam .. 12..
002.12A: kARena cakzuzA kim vA cakzuH-pIqA eva kevalam .. 12..
; kARa blind;  cakzus eye; pIqA pain (pIq to squeeze, to hurt)
; kevalam only

002.11-12E: What is the good of (what benefit can accrue from) having a son who is neither learned nor pious (dutiful); (for) what is the use of an eye that is blind? It simply causes occular pain.

002.13F: ajAtamftamUrKARAM varamAdyO na cAntimaH .
002.13A: ajAta-mfta-mUrKARAm varam AdyO na ca antimaH .
; varam better; Adya du. first (two); antima last

002.14F: sakfdduHKakarAvAdyAvantimastu pade pade .. 13..
002.14A: sakft duHKa-karO AdyO antimaH tu pade pade .. 13..
; sakft at once; 
002.14P: sakfdekavAram .

002.13-14E: Of sons, not born, (born and) dead and foolish, the first two are to be preferred and not the last: (for) the first two cause pain (but) once ; the last at every step.

002.15F: kiM ca . sa jAto yena jAtena yAti vaMSaH samunnatim .
002.15A: kim ca . saH jAtaH yena jAtena yAti vaMSaH samunnatim .
; vaMSa lineage; sam-ud-nati rising, elevation

002.16F: parivartini saMsAre mftaH ko vA na jAyate .. 14..
002.16A: parivartini saMsAre mftaH kaH vA na jAyate .. 14..
; parivartin ever-recurring, revolving; saMsAra the (secular) world; 
002.15-16E: Moreover . He is (really) born by whose birth the family is exalted. In this revolving world who does not die and is not born again?

; Kale translates kaWinI as 'little finger'? MW 'chalk'
002.17F: guRigaRagaRanAramBe na patati kaWinI susamBramAdyasya .
002.17A: (guRi-gaRa)-gaRana-AramBe na patati kaWinI susamBramAt yasya .
; guRi-gaRa count of virtuous (persons); gaRana counting;
; AramBa beginning; kaWinI little finger (Ap90) ('chalk' in MW)
; susamBramma great hurry
002.17P: guRigaRaga° -- guRAH ezAM vidyante iti guRinaH tezAM gaRaH tasya gaRanA tasyAH aramBe
002.17P: kaWinI -- kanizWikA

002.18F: tenAmbA yadi sutinI vada vanDyA kIdfSI nAma .. 15..
002.18A: tena ambA yadi sutinI vada vanDyA kIdfSI nAma .. 15..
; ambA mother; sutinI mother (of a son); vanDyA barren (woman) [cf. ap90 baMDya]
; nAma (after an interr.) what then?
002.18P: guRigaRagaRanAramBe yasya [putrasya kfte] kaWinI susaMBramAt na patati tena putreRa yadi ambA tajjananI sutinI praSastaputravatI Bavet tarhi vaMDyA kIdfSI nAma Bavet iti SezaH . yasyAH putraH guRinAM na DurIRaH sA vaMDyA eva iti BAvaH .

002.17-18E: If the mother of the boy, for whom the little finger does not bend down hastily at the commencement of the enumeration of the number of meritorious men, be said to have given birth to a son, then say, what a barren woman would be like to (i.e., she is as good as a barren woman).

002.19F: dAne tapasi SOrye ca yasya na praTitaM yaSaH .
002.19A: dAne tapasi SOrye ca yasya na praTitam yaSaH .
; dAna donation, charity ; tapas austerity; SOrya heroism;
; praT ; praTita spread; yaSas fame
; 
002.20F: vidyAyAmarTalABe ca mAturuccAra eva saH .. 16..
002.20A: vidyAyAm arTalABe ca mAtuH uccAraH eva saH .. 16..
; arTa-laBa wealth-attainment; uc-cAra discharge, excrement

002.19-20E: He, who is not well known for his charity, penance, bravery, learning and the acquisition of wealth, is but the excrement of his mother.

002.21F: aparaM ca . varameko guRI putro na ca mUrKaSatAnyapi .
002.21A: aparaM ca . varam ekaH guRI putraH na ca mUrKaSatAni api .

002.22F: ekaScandrastamo hanti na ca tArAgaRo'pi ca .. 17..
002.22A: ekaH candraH tamaH hanti na ca tArA-gaRaH api ca .. 17..

002.21-22E: Also, It is better to have one meritorious son than a hundred of foolish ones; the single moon dispels darkness; and not the whole firmament of stars.

002.23F: puRyatIrTe kftaM yena tapaH kvApyatiduzkaram .
002.23A: puRya-tIrTe kftam yena tapaH kva api atiduzkaram .
; puRya virtue; tIrTa path; kvApi somewhere; ati-duzkara very arduous;
002.23P: puRyatIrTe -- puRyaM ca tat tIrTaM ca tasmin . karma .

002.24F: tasya putro BavedvaSyaH samfdDo DArmikaH suDIH .. 18..

011.17-18E: For. Very great is the distance that separates the body from the qualities: the body is liable to destruction in a moment, while the qualities endure to the end of the universe.

023.20P: jarAparigataH jarayABiBUtaH san .

023.16-20E: Manthara said . Riches are comparable to (as unsteady as) the dust of the feet; youth flies away with the rapidity of a mountain river; life is as fleeting as a rolling drop of water, and existence as evanascent as foam. (such being the case) he, who, with his judgment deprived, does not perform his religious duties, which unfasten the bolt of the gate of heaven, being overtaken by old age and full of contrition, is burnt by the fire of sorrow.

024.18-19E: There was a hunter, Bhairava by name, residing in the province of Kalyana. He, one day, went to the Vindhya forest in search of a deer. As he passed carrying the deer that he had killed, he saw a boar of a formidable form.

032.34-35E: The greatness of what man that looks lower and lower (i. e. looks upon himself as a very small man or looks at those who are in a humbler station) does not increase? But every one who looks higher and higher (i. e. considers himself as very great, or turns his eyes upon those who are in a higher station) becomes poor.

033.01-02E: Moreover. A man who has abundant wealth, although he be a Brahmana-killer, is respected; while one, although claiming a pedigree as noble as that of the moon, is despised, if without wealth.

033.03-04E: Again. The goddess of wealth does not wish to embrace (favour) him who is not industrious, who is lazy, who trusts in fate and who is not enterprising, as a young woman does not an old husband.

033.05-06E: Also. Idleness, attendance on women, a diseased state, a fond partiality for one's native place, contentment, and cowardliness are the six impediments to greatness.

033.07-08E: For. When a man considers himself as happily situated, even with little wealth, Fate, I think, having done its duty, does not increase that wealth of his.

033.11-12E: It is also said. One should desire to obtain that which is unobtained, keep safe with judicious care what is obtained, properly increase what is preserved, and bestow the same on worthy recipients when it has been increased.

041.21-29E: Therefore, friend, give me your permission. I will go. Karataka said -- My blessing to you. May your path be auspicious (i. e. I wish you godspeed). Do as you desire. Damanaka then repaired into Pingalaka's presence like one amazed. Now, being respectfully received into his presence by the king, he prostrated himself before him, touching the ground with the eight parts of the body, and sat down. The king said -- You are seen after a long time. Damanaka replied -- Although Your Majesty has nothing to do with me as a servant, still a follower must necessarily attend upon his master when the time demands it, and hence have I come here. Moreover,

043.07-21E: Pingalaka said--Dear Damanaka, why do you talk so? You, the son of our prime minister, did not come here for so long a time believing in the words of some rogue. Now freely say your say. Damanaka said -- Lord, I have a question to ask. {;hitoeng050.txt}  Please reply. Why does my lord stand here, as if amazed, without drinking water, although thirsty ? Pingalaka replied -- You have spoken well. But there is no one trustworthy to whom this secret can be confined. You are such a one. Therefore I will communicate it to you. Listen. This forest has now been inhabited by some beast, unheard of before, and must for that reason, be left by us. I am perplexed on this account. Similarly you too have heard that strange loud sound. Great must be the strength of this animal corresponding to his voice. Damanaka replied -- My lord, this is, indeed, a great cause for fear. We too have heard the sound. But he is a bad minister who first counsels the quitting of land and then a fight. At this crisis when it is difficult to know what steps to take, the use of servants alone is to be known. For,

043.24-29E: The lion said -- Friend, a great terror has overtaken me. Damanaka said again (To himself --) How, else, can you talk to me of leaving the pleasures of a kingdom and going to another place. (Aloud) My lord, as long as I am alive, Your Majesty should have no fear. But Karataka and others should also be encouraged (by marks of royal favour), since it is difficult to have a united body of men at the time of overcoming a calamity.

043.30-35E: Then Damanaka and Karataka, on whom every honour was bestowed by the king, set out having promised to ward off the danger. On the way Karatake said to Damanaka -- Friend, without ascertaining whether the cause of fear is possible to be averted or not, why did you accept this great favour having undertaken the removal of the fear? For unless one has done a service one should not accept a reward from anybody, especially from a king. Observe,

044.01-07E: Damanaka smiled and said -- Friend, rest quiet (easy). I have known the cause of fear. That was the bellowing of a bull. Bulls form even our food, how much so of the lion then? Damanaka replied -- Had I relieved the king's fear just there, do you think that we could have received this great favour? Also,

059.22-23E: Death in battle, therefore, should be accepted. It will not be proper for me, now, to act in obedience to his commands. Because, If dead, he (a brave warrior) attains heaven; if he kills the foe he obtains happiness.

073.37-38E: Brahmanas are ruined when discontented, and kings when contented, a harlot full of modesty is ruined and so are ladies of family, if without modesty.

074.05-06E: Moreover, (The acquisition of) land, an ally and gold -- these three are the benefits accruing from war; when these can be counted upon as sure then only war should be made.

074.18-19E: What is the use of counsel given according to the Sastras (or, like the knowledge of the Sastras) to a king, if it be not acted upon? In no case can a disease be cured by the mere knowledge of medicine.

074.27-28E: In the rear should slowly march, O king, the commander-in-chief, accompained by ministers and brave warriors, cheering those that are fatigued and backing the army.

075.01-02E: One should traverse uneven ground abounding in water and full of hills by means of elephants, plains by means of horses, and rivers by means of boats, while the infantry should be employed in all place.

076.01-02E: That army they declare to be the best, the soldiers in which are naturally brave, skilled in the use of weapons, loyal (lit. attached to their master), inured to fatigue and mostly drawn from the ranks of renowned Kshatriyas.

076.03F: yaTA praBukftAnmAnAdyuDyante Buvi mAnavAH .

076.03-04E: As men fight in this world, O king, by honour being shown to them by their lord, so they do not, even by large sums of money being given to them.

076.05-06E: It is better to have a small army of chosen men than a multitude of heads: for the defeat of the weak will evidently lead to that of the strong.

076.09-10E: One wishing to gain victory should attack his enemies without hard-pressing his own army: for the army of the enemies, when extremely wearied by long marches, can be easily overpowered.

104.31-32E: The life of creatures is, indeed, as fleeting (lit. unsteady) as the reflection of the moon in water: knowing that it is such, one should always do what is (truly) beneficial.

105.25-28E: As long as the moon-crested god (Siva), the abode of the love of the Snow-mountain's daughter (Parvati) exists, as long as Lakshmi sports in the heart of Murari (Vishnu) like lightning flashing in the clouds; and as long as there exists the Gold-mountain (Meru) which resembles an (immense) wild fire and whose spark is the sun; so long may continue in circulation this collection of stories made by Narayana!!

105.29-30E: And lastly, May the prosperous king, Dhavalachandra, be victorious over his enemies; -- he, who with an effort, got this compendium of stories to be made and published!
